     299             : /* As with expanding/condensing, we are going to assume that LCG glyphs have
     300             :  * at most two counter zones, one near the bottom (baseline), one near the top.
     301             :  * So check if the given counter is intersected by some DStems at two positions:
     302             :  * 25% glyph height and 75% glyph height. If so, then only the "white" part
     303             :  * of the counter can be scaled by the normal counter ratio, while for the space
     304             :  * covered by DStems the stem ratio should be used instead.
     305             :  * However if at least one of the stems which form the counter doesn't extend
     306             :  * to the top/bottom part of the glyph (Latin "Y" is the most obvious example),
     307             :  * then the actual counter width in that part is larger than just the space
     308             :  * between two stems (or a stem and a glyph boundary), so that expanding just
     309             :  * that space would make the counter disproportionally wide. We are attempting
     310             :  * to compensate this by subtracting a half base stem width from the "white"
     311             :  * part of the counter
     312             :  */

    3109             : /* We need to look at the counters. There are two types of counters: */
    3110             : /*  the left and right side bearings */

    3112             : /* If the glyph is nicely hinted with vertical stems then all we need to */
    3113             : /*  do is look at the hints. Complications "B" which has slightly different */
    3114             : /*  counters top and bottom. */

    3116             : /*  near the bottom (baseline), one near the top */
    3117             : /* However many glyphs have diagonal stems: V, A, W, M, K, X, Y */
    3118             : /*  Many of these have two zones (like "B" above) W, M, K, Y (maybe X) */
    3119             : /* Find the places where these guys hit the baseline/cap-height (x-height) */
    3120             : /*  and define these as potential counter boundries. Ignore places where   */
    3121             : /*  glyphs hit with curves (like O, Q, p). */
    3122             : /* Remember to merge a hint with a top/bottom hit (harder with serifs) */
    3123             : 
    3124             : /* We may still not have a useful counter: 7 3 2 C E T */

    3756             :     /* When we do an expand stroke we expect that a glyph's bounding box will */
    3757             :     /*  increase by half the stroke width in each direction. Now we want to do*/
    3758             :     /*  different operations in each dimension. We don't want to increase the */
    3759             :     /*  x-height, or the cap height, whereas it is ok to make the glyph wider */
    3760             :     /*  but it would be nice to preserve the left and right side bearings. */
    3761             :     /* So shift the glyph over by width/2 (this preserves the left side bearing)*/
    3762             :     /* Increment the width by width (this preserves the right side bearing)   */
    3763             :     /* The y dimension is more complex. In a normal latin (greek, cyrillic)   */
    3764             :     /*  font the x-height is key, in a font with only capital letters it would*/
    3765             :     /*  be the cap-height. In the subset of the font containing superscripts  */
    3766             :     /*  we might want to key off of the superscript size. The expansion will  */
    3767             :     /*  mean that the glyph protrudes width/2 below the baseline, and width/2 */
    3768             :     /*  above the x-height and cap-height. Neither of those is acceptable. So */
    3769             :     /*  choose some intermediate level, say x-height/2, any point above this  */
    3770             :     /*  moves down by width/2, any point below this moves up by width/2 */
    3771             :     /* That'll work for many glyphs. But consider "o", depending on how it is */
    3772             :     /*  designed we might be moving the leftmost point either up or down when */
    3773             :     /*  it should remain near the center. So perhaps we have a band which is  */
    3774             :     /*  width wide right around x-height/2 and points in that band don't move */
    3775             :     /* Better. Consider a truetype "o" were there will be intermediate points */
    3776             :     /*  Between the top-most and left-most. These shouldn't move by the full */
    3777             :     /*  width/2. They should move by some interpolated amount. Based on the */
